ğŸ” Document Summary: AFCA Determinations on Improper Motor Policy Cancellations
This document contains summaries of selected AFCA determinations involving insurance claim denials based on policy cancellations, particularly where the cancellation process was disputed or not properly communicated. Across the decisions, AFCA repeatedly found in favour of consumers where:

ğŸ§· Key Patterns Identified in Determinations
1. No Clear Cancellation Notice Issued
In multiple cases, AFCA ruled that policy cancellation requires clear written communication, even if the consumer had previously expressed interest in cancelling.

If insurers or agents (e.g. brokers or lease managers like SG Fleet) did not follow up or confirm the cancellation properly, AFCA upheld the complaints and ordered claim payouts.

2. Inconsistent Communication or Administrative Failures
Where the insurer or intermediary gave conflicting information, or internal records showed the policy as active, AFCA found that consumers had no reason to believe their cover had lapsed.

3. Reliance on System/Invoice Silence
In some cases, insurers argued that "missing charges" or invoice changes implied cancellation. AFCA rejected this unless clearly explained to the customer, particularly where previous invoices included bundled charges.

4. Delegated Administration (Like SG Fleet)
In several rulings, AFCA emphasised that if the underwriter delegates administration, they remain responsible for ensuring legal compliance and procedural fairness, especially if claim denial is based on that administration.

5. Misleading Conduct & Duty of Care
Silence, ambiguous documentation, or failure to correct misapprehensions were seen as potentially misleading conduct under the ACL or failure to act with reasonable care.

6. Outcome: Claim Paid + Compensation
In most cases where AFCA found fault, the insurer was required to honour the claim and pay compensation for distress and inconvenience, sometimes ranging from $1,000 to over $3,000.
